### Post by Nano Geek on 2007-12-01
December 2007 Desktops - Posting Guidelines

* Stay within the board rules, no matter how hot you may believe the wallpaper/screen shot to be.

* If you are going to quote, there isn't a need to quote an img-embeded picture - Just don't do it. Please just reference the post by page number/page link/etc.

* Off Topic Posts will be edited or removed.

* The desktops thread is not to be used as a means to post explicit or suggestive, and provocative images (they must be safe for your kids and/or boss to see). Please help to keep the thread relevant and safe to browse for everyone.

* The moderators of this forum reserve the right to edit or remove your posts as necessary so they may comply with our Community Rule set.

* Please use reduced-size thumbnails, where possible, out of respect for people running on lower bandwidth or screen resolutions.

*To avoid having users having to ask you for them. we request that you format your posts in the following order:

Themes: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).

Wallpaper: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).

Icons: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).

Programs: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).

Important Note: Any image posted that is over 800 x 600 will be removed! Use a thumbnail or use a text link to your image. If your image is removed, this is why.

---

### Post by SomeGuyDude on 2007-12-01
Pissing around with making my desktop kinda OSX-y. I have yet to find any dark themes that blend together well (I find an emerald theme I love, a GTK theme I love, but they look like balls together), and considering I'm on battery power with dimmed display I went lighter.

Basically all the first responses you get for "OSX" on gnome-look.org, plus AWN with the chrome-type theme, plus a background I found on DeviantART.

Need to throw a few desklets on there, though, I'm thinking about the Cairo Clock, mainly. Of course, if I do that, I need a new wallpaper. That would just look ridiculous.

### Post by AlexR1 on 2007-12-01
> **What is in a name? said:**
> Oh, and that bottom panel puzzles me, it's so interesting... Doesn't even look like GNOME... How did you do it?

I put two panels on top of each other, bottom panel is 40 pixels high and i have multiline taskbar,and top panel is just a 15 pixels high.
Both panels are set to transparent and background images are loaded, to get that look like on screenshot.If you need more sand me your e-mail and i can send you a backgrounds so you can set your panels to look the same.I don`t know is this relevant but i am using Ubuntu 7.10 (Gutsy Gibbon).

### Post by gamma on 2007-12-01
> **fedex1993 said:**
> how is kde4 i tryed to install but faild pretty badly.
It's a pretty awesome DE and everything works great. The applications are pretty crashy right now (Konqueror, Kopete, Kmail specifically), but I use Firefox and Gmail for email so that's not an issue for me.

Dolphin is a great filemanager, It's got some pretty cool fade/hover effects and the split folder view is pretty cool. Kwin has expose like effects built in too which is cool.

Have you tried building via kdesvn-build? If you're moderately experienced in messing with the command line it's a great way to preview KDE4.

---

### Post by fedex1993 on 2007-12-01
> **gamma said:**

Dolphin is a great filemanager, It's got some pretty cool fade/hover effects and the split folder view is pretty cool. Kwin has expose like effects built in too which is cool.

Have you tried building via kdesvn-build? If you're moderately experienced in messing with the command line it's a great way to preview KDE4.

is there a tutorials some where on how to kdesvn-build? because i did the live cd and then i also got just regular ubuntu with gnome stock and then tried the live cd worked but crashed ever 3 sec

---

### Post by gamma on 2007-12-01
> **fedex1993 said:**
> is there a tutorials some where on how to kdesvn-build? because i did the live cd and then i also got just regular ubuntu with gnome stock and then tried the live cd worked but crashed ever 3 sec

There's an ubuntu thread on it right now.
[http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=609075&highlight=kde4](http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=609075&highlight=kde4)

Basically follow the Kubuntu section here (use apt-get instead of aptitude if on Ubuntu):
[http://techbase.kde.org/Getting_Started/Build/KDE4#Kubuntu_and_Debian](http://techbase.kde.org/Getting_Started/Build/KDE4#Kubuntu_and_Debian)

Once you get the dependencies installed follow the kdesvn-build guide from the bookmarked place on.
[http://techbase.kde.org/Getting_Started/Build/kdesvn-build#Download_and_install_kdesvn-build](http://techbase.kde.org/Getting_Started/Build/kdesvn-build#Download_and_install_kdesvn-build)

After you get everything up and running updating to the latest version of kde4 is as easy as typing ./kdesvn-build :P. Of course compiling takes a little while, so don't expect to have kde4 up and running in an hour. Any build related questions I'd suggest replying in that thread (or send me a PM), no need to fill up the screenshot thread with installation chat :P.

---

[http://techbase.kde.org/Getting_Started/Build/KDE4#Kubuntu_and_Debian](http://techbase.kde.org/Getting_Started/Build/KDE4#Kubuntu_and_Debian)

Once you get the dependencies installed follow the kdesvn-build guide from the bookmarked place on.
[http://techbase.kde.org/Getting_Started/Build/kdesvn-build#Download_and_install_kdesvn-build](http://techbase.kde.org/Getting_Started/Build/kdesvn-build#Download_and_install_kdesvn-build)

After you get everything up and running updating to the latest version of kde4 is as easy as typing ./kdesvn-build :P. Of course compiling takes a little while, so don't expect to have kde4 up and running in an hour. Any build related questions I'd suggest replying in that thread (or send me a PM), no need to fill up the screenshot thread with installation chat :P.
ty very much and thanks

---

### Post by p_quarles on 2007-12-02
> **nathangrubb said:**
> I don't understand how everyone elses fluxbox looks awesome yet I still haven't managed to get a desktop background yet....maybe I'm not deep enough into it
It's easy, you just have to know where to look:
```
fbsetbg -f /path/to/image
```
That's temporary, but you can add it to the startup file to make it automatic.

### Post by crimesaucer on 2007-12-03
> **What is in a name? said:**
> I know this must be a very basic question by now, but none of the tutorials I followed allowed me to change my Xfce-panel background. Does anyone here, especially other Xfce die-hard fans, know how to replace the usual background color, inherited from the GTK theme of the moment, with another color or picture?... Thanks...

To use an image as the background for the xfce4-panel, you will have to use a separate gtkrc-2.0

1st: Make an image, and save it as panel.png

(I make my images 1 pixel wide so there is a consistent even flow)

2nd: Make a .gtkrc-2.0 and save it into ~/

here is my gtkrc-2.0 :

```

style "panel"
{
  bg[NORMAL] = "#000000"
  bg_pixmap[NORMAL] = "panel.png"
  fg[NORMAL] = "#FFFFFF"
  }

widget_class "*Panel*"      style "panel"
widget "*Panel*"            style "panel"
class "*Panel*"             style "panel"

```


3rd: Then in "alt+f2" run:

```
killall xfce4-panel
``` 

next type "alt+f2" again and run:

```
xfce4-panel &
```  

to restart your xfce4-panel using your new gtkrc-2.0 (or just skip all of that and just restart your computer after doing step 1 and 2).

---

### Post by crimesaucer on 2007-12-03
> **What is in a name? said:**
> Thanks!!

Just a wild question... It is not possible to put an image with transparencies as a background, or is it?...

No. whatever image you use, it will be a 0% transparency. But you can make your panel 10% or 20% transparent. My image is a black glossy panel and I have it at 36% transparent, and my icons still look pretty good. You can see the wallpaper behind it, and the buttons are still readable.

Large View: [http://i144.photobucket.com/albums/r161/crimesaucer/Screenshot-116panel.png](http://i144.photobucket.com/albums/r161/crimesaucer/Screenshot-116panel.png)
[IMG]http://i144.photobucket.com/albums/r161/crimesaucer/Screenshot-116panel-1.png[/IMG]

---

### Post by What is in a name? on 2007-12-03
> **crimesaucer said:**
> No. whatever image you use, it will be a 0% transparency. But you can make your panel 10% or 20% transparent. My image is a black glossy panel and I have it at 36% transparent, and my icons still look pretty good. You can see the wallpaper behind it, and the buttons are still readable.

Large View: [http://i144.photobucket.com/albums/r161/crimesaucer/Screenshot-116panel.png](http://i144.photobucket.com/albums/r161/crimesaucer/Screenshot-116panel.png)
[IMG]http://i144.photobucket.com/albums/r161/crimesaucer/Screenshot-116panel-1.png[/IMG]

### Post by billgoldberg on 2007-12-03
So after having internet and synaptic issues, and the fact all my data is backed up on an external hd, i've reinstalled gutsy (only took 20 min).

So I'll repost my desktop.

[[img]http://xs322.xs.to/xs322/07491/one.png.xs.jpg[/img]](http://xs.to/xs.php?h=xs322&d=07491&f=one.png)

[[img]http://xs122.xs.to/xs122/07491/two.png.xs.jpg[/img]](http://xs.to/xs.php?h=xs122&d=07491&f=two.png)

[[img]http://xs122.xs.to/xs122/07491/three.png.xs.jpg[/img]](http://xs.to/xs.php?h=xs122&d=07491&f=three.png)

**GTK2 Theme:**
WII-Black (gnome look)

**Icon Set: **
black and white icons (gnome look)

**Curved AWN**

**Wallpaper:**
from deviant art

**XMMS skin:**
Kore (gnome art)

**XMMS icon:**
[here]("http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?p=3868313")

**Conky file:**
```
background yes
use_xft no
xftfont Bitstream Vera Sans:size=7
xftalpha 0.8
update_interval 0.5
own_window yesEdit/Delete Message  
own_window_type normal
own_window_transparent yes
own_window_hints undecorated,below,sticky,skip_taskbar,skip_pager
double_buffer yes
draw_shades no
draw_outline no
draw_border no
draw_graph_borders yes
stippled_borders no
default_color white
default_shade_color black
alignment top_right
minimum_size 1425
maximum_width 1425
gap_y 32
gap_x 32
use_spacer no
no_buffers yes

TEXT
${color white} Ubuntu $sysname $kernel${alignr} Processors - Intel Core2 Duo - ${cpu cpu0}% ${cpugraph cpu1 8, 30 ffffff ffffff} ${cpugraph cpu2 8, 30 ffffff ffffff} | Memory - ${mem} of ${memmax} ${memgraph mem 8, 30 ffffff ffffff} | Processes - $running_processes of $processes running | HDD - ${fs_used /} of ${fs_size /} used | Wireless - ${addr eth1} - ${downspeed ra0} kbps down ${downspeedgraph eth1 8,30} ${upspeed eth1} kbps up ${downspeedgraph eth1 8,30}
```

note: i didn't make the conky file, i ripped it from the "post your .conkyrc" thread.

### Post by p_quarles on 2007-12-07
> **taisao said:**
> :confused: How did you get the context/popup menu with applications?
In KDE, go to Control Center >> Desktop >> Behavior. Modify one of your mouse buttons to open a "Custom Menu," and it will prompt you to create said menu.

### Post by epimer on 2007-12-08
So, my [previous post]("http://ubuntuforums.org ol/showthread.php?p=3901381#post3901381") in here had my trying out Xfce, mostly because I missed GTK theming and was curious to know what GTK apps I was missing out on (from my old Gnome days). So this is for the "anything you can do, K can do better" file :P Well, not quite. ### Post by andrek on 2007-12-08
No guys, it comes with desktop-base package.
It's located in /usr/share/images/desktop-base/

### Post by yabbadabbadont on 2007-12-09
> **el mariachi said:**
> If anyone knows how to change that ugly clock from fbpanel please do say something

You will need to edit your ~/.fbpanel/default config file (or whatever you called it).  Change the plugin from dclock to tclock to get a standard, bold text based clock display.  Here is the section from my config as an example:
```
Plugin {
    type = tclock
    config {
        ClockFmt = %l:%M %p
        TooltipFmt = %a %b %e, %Y
        Action = calendar-display &
    }
}

```
**calendar-display**:
```
#!/usr/bin/env bash

cal -3 | xmessage -fg black -bg gray75 -default okay -geometry -0-30 -fn "-xos4-terminus-bold-r-normal-*-*-160-*-*-*-*-iso10646-1" -title "Three Month Calendar" -file - &
```
Of course, you will probably want to change the font and colors used.

---

### Post by jordanmthomas on 2007-12-10
> **Sam Plamondon said:**
> How do you get screen shots of the Desktop Cube?

I use scrot to take my screenshots.
```
scrot -d 5 /path/to/save.png
```
Will wait 5 seconds and then take a screenshot.

Also, ksnapshot can do this.
Also, the gimp has a facility to do it (in its file menu somewhere)

---

### Post by alwiap on 2007-12-10
> **Sam Plamondon said:**
> How do you get screen shots of the Desktop Cube?

just like normal, click 'print screen' on the keyboard when you have the desktop cube in view

### Post by sunexplodes on 2007-12-11
Okay, here goes. I've put together my first "dark" theme. I usually don't care for them, but I found a dark emerald theme that I loved, but it didn't go with my lighter theme, so I thought I'd give it a try.

[ATTACH]52866[/ATTACH]

DE: KDE 3.5x
WM: ([AKONKOLOR](http://www.kde-look.org/content/show.php/AXONKOLOR?content=54899&PHPSESSID=affe99c37f67593834d8278906bdeee1)) Emerald
STYLE: a custom Domino config/colorscheme. 
ICONS: Various, from the Breathless, Crystal Project, and Mac4Lin themes, as well as a few others from around the web. 
FONTS: Mostly the Lucida family, as well as Heldustry for the allcaps stuff.

I'd be more than happy to upload my dominorc, color scheme, or any other part of this theme if anyone wants.

### Post by PurposeOfReason on 2007-12-11
> **fedex1993 said:**
> what bar are you using at the bottom it looks really nice and i like it
That is tint task manager (ttm). Google it. But for it to work like I have it, you need revision 20 (anything newer only makes a space betwwen the bottom and the actual box and there is nothing better after 20 anyways)  and my tintrc.

GET IT
 ```
svn checkout -r 20 http://ttm.googlecode.com/svn/trunk/ ttm-read-only
```

~/.config/tint/tintrc
```

font = UnBatang 9
font_color = #e0e0e0font = UnBatang 9
font_color = #e0e0e0
font_alpha = 60
font_active_color = #e0e0e0
font_active_alpha = 100
font_shadow = 0

task_text_centered = 1
task_width = 120
task_margin = 6
task_padding = 6

task_background = 1
task_background_color = #262626
task_background_alpha = 42
task_active_background_color = #262626
task_active_background_alpha = 70
task_background_as_border = 1

panel_width = 0
panel_height = 15
panel_tasks_centered = 0

panel_background = 0
panel_background_color = #ffffff
panel_background_alpha = 60
font_alpha = 60
font_active_color = #e0e0e0
font_active_alpha = 100
font_shadow = 0

task_text_centered = 1
task_width = 120
task_margin = 6
task_padding = 6

task_background = 1
task_background_color = #262626
task_background_alpha = 42
task_active_background_color = #262626
task_active_background_alpha = 70
task_background_as_border = 1

panel_width = 0
panel_height = 15
panel_tasks_centered = 0

panel_background = 0
panel_background_color = #ffffff
panel_background_alpha = 60
```

---

### Post by jryprt on 2007-12-12
> **pavit_laul said:**
> hey! how did you get the temperature at the top?
Right click on top panel click on Add to panel look for weather report
drag & drop to top panel 
then right click on the weather icon in top panel click on preferences
click on location type in your city 
set the stuff in the general tab

### Post by santiagoward2000 on 2007-12-12
> **floke said:**
> Nice terminal effect - howd'ya do that?

First, I set transparency and removed the borders. Then, I put it in that angle using Compiz-Fusion's **freewins** plugin.
It's an unofficial plugin, but if you want to install it, I used this guide:
[http://forum.compiz-fusion.org/showthread.php?t=5303]("http://forum.compiz-fusion.org/showthread.php?t=5303")

---

### Post by floke on 2007-12-12

### Post by santiagoward2000 on 2007-12-12
> **averagebeatboy said:**
> santiagoward2000,

How did you get the really large and awesome looking icons on the right side of your desktop?

Averagebeatboy

I'm using Xfce. All I had to do is right click on the desktop, click on **Desktop Settings...** and increase the **Icon size** under the **Behavior** tab.
The icon theme is **Dropline Neu!**, which is inside the **gnome-extra-icons** package, in Ubuntu's repository.
Cheers!

_EDIT:_
:oops: Sorry! Did you mean the sidebar? They're [Screenlets]("www.screenlets.org").
You can find the installation instructions in the FAQ.

### Post by santiagoward2000 on 2007-12-12
> **averagebeatboy said:**
> santiagoward2000,

The screenlets were what I was talking about THEY ARE SOOOO AWESOME AND will keep me busy for days.

Thank you so much.

Synaptic installed the Gnome-Extra-Icons.  I was just wondering where  Synaptic put them and how do I USE them.

Thanks again,

Averagebeatboy

Ahh, they are installed in **usr/share/icons**, and to use them, just go to **Applications / Settings / User Interface Settings** (at least in Xubuntu, I'm not sure where this is in Ubuntu).
You can also change the theme here, and you can install more themes with the **gnome-themes-extras** package...

---

### Post by ~LoKe on 2007-12-13
> **shearn89 said:**
> Is that screen you're using for the info line at the bottom of ncmpc? If so, whats the config/settings for it?

Oh, and what console-based messenger program are you using (i'm looking at the workspace-type info at the bottom of you're term)?

Yep, screen indeed.  Centericq is the messenger (supports all protocols, not just icq).  Here's my .screenrc:

> startup_message off
vbell           off
defscrollback   512
shell           -$SHELL
shelltitle      sh
autodetach      on

# enable SHIFT-PGUP / SHIFT-PGDOWN scroll
termcapinfo rxvt ti@:te@

# change window with ALT-. ALT-,
bindkey "^[," prev
bindkey "^[." next

# change window with ALT-Q ALT-W
bindkey "^[q" prev
bindkey "^[w" next

# keyboard shortcuts
bind ^a screen -t bash             # C-a-a
bind ^m screen -t mpd  ncmpc         # C-a-m
bind ^i screen -t messenger  centericq     # C-a-i
bind ^r screen -t rtorrent rtorrent          # C-arf
#bind ^s screen -t fxp0 slurm -i fxp0 # C-a-s

# startup sessions
screen -t messenger 0 centericq
screen -t rtorrent 1 rtorrent
screen -t mpd 2 ncmpc
screen -t bash 3
# select 0

# status // change %{= M} --> %{= kM} to display status on black background
hardstatus alwayslastline '%{= M} %H%{= G} %l %= %{= w}%-w%{+b r}%n*%t%{-b r}%{w}%+w %= %{c}%d %D %{B}%c '

# add CPU idle/sustem/user/interrupt stats
backtick 100 5 5 tail -1 /var/tmp/vermaden-stats-top
caption always '%{= wk} %= %100` %='

# F1-F4 switch
# bindkey -k k1 select 1
# bindkey -k k2 select 2
# bindkey -k k3 select 3
# bindkey -k k4 select 4

---

### Post by jr.gotti on 2007-12-13
> **~LoKe said:**
> DWM!

...My hats off to you man. I just compiled DWM, and it's friggin hideous. NO IDEA how you got it looking so nice.

Any chance on getting a guide to achieve similiar results to what you have here?

(IE, the fading menubar, the "border" around open applications, the general "awesome" look you have going on here?)

Until then...back to fluxbox for me...this is ridiculous.

---

### Post by ~LoKe on 2007-12-13
> **jr.gotti said:**
> ...My hats off to you man. I just compiled DWM, and it's friggin hideous. NO IDEA how you got it looking so nice.

Any chance on getting a guide to achieve similiar results to what you have here?

(IE, the fading menubar, the "border" around open applications, the general "awesome" look you have going on here?)

Until then...back to fluxbox for me...this is ridiculous.

The fading menubar was a byproduct of running xcompmgr -cCfF.  The effect was nice but I didn't want it, so I don't use it anymore.  As for window borders, well, it should all be within the first few lines of config.h.  Here are the relevant lines:

> #define BARPOS                  BarTop /* BarBot, BarOff */
#define BORDERPX                        2
#define FONT                            "-*-bitstream vera sans mono-medium-r-normal-*-10-*-*-*-*-*-*-*"
#define NORMBORDERCOLOR "#222222"
#define NORMBGCOLOR             "#222222"
#define NORMFGCOLOR             "#cccccc"
#define SELBORDERCOLOR  "#222222"
#define SELBGCOLOR              "#222222"
#define SELFGCOLOR              "#afc81c"
#define TOPBAR                  True            /* False */

The rest of config.h is basically how you want your windows positioned, tagging, key bindings, etc.

### Post by Mr.Auer on 2007-12-13
My desktop doesnt look much like the default Ubuntu :)

Im running Compiz Fusion with most of the plugins enabled (added compizconfig-manager) at 1600x1200 resolution. Metacity theme is Vicious Apple window decorations with Murrine-Kent controls, icons are Snowish Mac icons. 

First ive removed the upper panel, and lower gnome panel is host to only the system tray, and its normally hidden in the lower right, with only hide button visible. 

I use Avant Window Navigator as the panel replacement. It also has a main menu, console and weather applets on. Only big bug ive noted in it presently is that if i select "move to another workspace" it crashes both nautilus and AWN :) Not nice...

Gkrellm outputs all sensors data, date and CPU and disk usage, and has the volume controls and XMMS control panel. My keyboard also has multimedia keys, which do all kindsa things from opening a terminal to shutting down the comp.

The background changes often according to my mood :) The present one is afaik from InterfaceLift, who have lots of highres backgrounds.

As you can see, I hate clutter and like my desktop to be as simple and as beautiful as possible. Eycandy ill eat any day...My desktop rarely has more icons than this, except when im working on some project. I tend to move all the stuff in their respective folders as soon as I have something done ready.

### Post by arbulus on 2007-12-13
> **new2*buntu said:**
> I am thinking about trying AWN. Is it that dock thing at the bottom of many of your desktops? What is it's purpose? Is it just a program launcher?


Yeah, if you're familiar with the dock on the Mac, it's very similar.  It houses launchers, but it's also a task manager - the launcher itself serves at the task.  It's really handy to keep launchers and the task manager in such a compact and nice looking spot.  You can also add other things to it like your Gnome Menu, a clock, system tray, etc.  You have to be running a compositor (like Compiz Fusion or xcompmgr) to run it though.

---

### Post by rjmdomingo2003 on 2007-12-14
> **fuscia said:**
> hey, rjm, could you post your tint file?
Here's my tintrc file:
```
font = UnDotum 9.3
font_color = #266867
font_alpha = 70
font_active_color = #081f3a
font_active_alpha = 100

task_text_centered = 1
task_width = 100
task_margin = 3
task_padding = 5

panel_width = 0
panel_height = 25
panel_tasks_centered = 1
panel_background = 1
panel_background_color = #081f3a
panel_background_alpha = 15

task_background = 1
task_background_color = #ffffff
task_background_alpha = 10
task_active_background_color = #ffffff
task_active_background_alpha = 20
task_background_as_border = 0



```

### Post by Whiffle on 2007-12-15
KDE 3.5.7
KORE theme (found on kde-look.org)
normal taskbar/kicker at top of screen


universal sidebar on right side, hidden at bottom:
[http://www.resnet.trinity.edu/avaselaa/temp1.png](http://www.resnet.trinity.edu/avaselaa/temp1.png)

universal sidebar on right side, unhidden.  Instant access to RSS feeds, bookmarks, devices, directories, amarok, etc.  I love it, definitely one of my favorite kde features.

### Post by What is in a name? on 2007-12-17
> **herbster said:**
> How do you get amarok colours to change? I mean the Engage, Playlist, etc. menubar and bottom statusbar. The "inside" of it changes via Appearance in settings but I'd like to grey the whole thing like yours as my gtk is similar and they would match. I run kde-config and nothing seems to happen. Is it about installing KDE?

Amarok, as all KDE apps, obbeys to the settings we make at the KControl. Install it by typing "sudo apt-get install kcontrol", and when you run it you'll have a section for colour schemes, along with themes, styles, etc. You do not need to install the whole KDE packages available. Or do you already have KControl installed?

---

### Post by fuscia on 2007-12-17

---

### Post by Mateo on 2007-12-17
> **fuscia said:**
> LOL! i don't even know what tagging is.

dwm does it too, not sure how though.  tags are sort of like  virtual desktops.  you can pick a window (in wmii) and press Alt+Shift+2 to make it move to "2".  You can also do more advanced stuff from the terminal that will tag certain applications (like your web browser, email client, irc client) as "web".  so when you have those programs launched, they will appear as a tag in the status bar.  it's the same concept as image tagging.  but like I said before, these WMs are tough to get used to.

---

### Post by samjh on 2007-12-17
Gnome with Compiz-Fusion and Emerald theme manager.

The theme is custom-made.  I call it BlueGem, using the default Beryl Red theme as base but with different colour, shadow, and transparency settings.  Engine is vrunner.

The widget set is a tweaked version of Glossy with darker shades of blue.

Icon set is Tango.

### Post by fedex1993 on 2007-12-19
> **fuscia said:**
> dwm (recompiled for color changes), urxvt, htop, mpd+ncmpc and scrot. the wallpaper was made from one of those yahoo most emailed pics.

what is the bar at the top and how did you get urxvt to look like that it looks awsome

---

### Post by fuscia on 2007-12-19
> **fedex1993 said:**
> what is the bar at the top and how did you get urxvt to look like that it looks awsome

thanks. the bar is the default toolbar (though, i did change the color) of dwm. i set up the look for urxvt in .Xdefaults.

here's my .Xdefaults file
 
```

! rxvt-unicode
URxvt*font: xft:"Baekmuk Batang":pixelsize=8
URxvt*scrollBar: False
URxvt*saveLines: 5000
URxvt*inheritPixmap: False
URxvt*geometry: 54x12
URxvt*background:      #590000
URxvt*foreground:      white
```

---

### Post by fedex1993 on 2007-12-19
> **fuscia said:**
> thanks. the bar is the default toolbar (though, i did change the color) of dwm. i set up the look for urxvt in .Xdefaults.

here's my .Xdefaults file
 
```

! rxvt-unicode
URxvt*font: xft:"Baekmuk Batang":pixelsize=8
URxvt*scrollBar: False
URxvt*saveLines: 5000
URxvt*inheritPixmap: False
URxvt*geometry: 54x12
URxvt*background:      #590000
URxvt*foreground:      white
```

ty fuscia thanks i love using urxvt i just never found out how to customize it

### Post by lzfy on 2007-12-21

---

### Post by gamma on 2007-12-21
> **lzfy said:**
> Nice. Is KDE4 stable to use? And which distro are you using?
KDE4 is really stable right now. Konqueror doesn't crash anymore and Kopete actually works. Plasma sometimes dies here or there, but it'll auto-restart itself and you won't lose any data in the process.

I'm using Ubuntu 7.10, but I'm using kdesvn-build to compile KDE4 via SVN. If you don't want/need bleeding edge builds I'd recommend checking out RC2 by adding the Kubuntu KDE4 repo (kubuntu.org and this will work with Ubuntu too).

---

### Post by fedex1993 on 2007-12-21
> **PurposeOfReason said:**
> Details in Abiword. :)

is there anyway that you might be able to psot your .Xdefaults for urxvt because yours is very noice

---

### Post by PurposeOfReason on 2007-12-21
> **fedex1993 said:**
> is there anyway that you might be able to psot your .Xdefaults for urxvt because yours is very noice
Of course:
```
URxvt.termName: rxvt
URxvt.transparent: true
URxvt.inheritPixmap: False
URxvt.imLocale: pl_PL.UTF-8
URxvt.scrollBar: false
URxvt.saveLines: 500
URxvt.urlLauncher:      firefox
URxvt.cursorBlink: true
URxvt.geometry: 80x17
URxvt.fading: 25%
urxvt.font:             xft:Bitstream Vera Sans Mono:pixelsize=9
urxvt.boldFont:         xft:Bitstream Vera Sans Mono:bold:pixelsize=10
#URxvt*background:      #000000
urxvt.depth: 32
urxvt.background: rgba:0000/0000/0000/dddd
URxvt.foreground: grey80
URxvt.tintColor: #262626
URxvt.borderLess: true
URxvt.borderColor: #888888

*foreground:     rgba:0000/0000/0000/dddd
*background:     rgb:10/10/10
!black
*color0:         rgb:20/20/20
*color8:         rgb:75/77/73
!red
*color1:         rgb:cc/00/00  
*color9:         rgb:ef/29/29
!green
*color2:         rgb:4e/9a/06
*color10:        rgb:8a/e2/34
!brown/yellow
*color3:         rgb:c4/a0/00
*color11:        rgb:fc/e9/4f
!blue
*color4:         rgb:34/65/a4
*color12:        rgb:72/9f/cf
!magenta
*color5:         rgb:75/50/7b
*color13:        rgb:ad/7f/a8
!cyan
*color6:         rgb:06/98/9a
*color14:        rgb:34/e2/e2
!white
*color7:         rgb:d3/d7/cf
*color15:        rgb:ee/ee/ec
```

---

> **gamma said:**
> KDE4 is really stable right now. Konqueror doesn't crash anymore and Kopete actually works. Plasma sometimes dies here or there, but it'll auto-restart itself and you won't lose any data in the process.

I'm using Ubuntu 7.10, but I'm using kdesvn-build to compile KDE4 via SVN. If you don't want/need bleeding edge builds I'd recommend checking out RC2 by adding the Kubuntu KDE4 repo (kubuntu.org and this will work with Ubuntu too).

Thanks. I tried the RC2 packages but it didn't work that great. But maybe it was my setup. I'll wait a little bit more, the final should be out soon :)

### Post by BobCFC on 2007-12-22
> **Onyros said:**
> Don't worry, you'll get the hang of it. Just make sure you copy the .awesomerc example to your home folder, and then start customizing.

You'll get hooked pretty soon. I still have to find out how to enable transparency in non-focused windows (option is there, I just can't get it enabled) and a few other things, but I really like it so far.



Still learning myself.   The documentation is really spartan.  

Try for transparency:
```

sudo apt-get install xcompmgr

xcompmgr -nc &
```

where n is for normal transparency and c is for shadows



Of course to use it you need to set background picture underneath otherwise no point lol:

```
sudo apt-get install feh

feh --bg-scale ~/Pictures/candy/background1.jpg 

```

#feh --bg-center or  --bg-scale or  --bg-tile  or --bg-seamless


these work fine from xterm but i'm still debugging getting things working automatically when it starts.

without using gdm to login (startx) you can control startup with** .xinitrc**

has a line such as   **exec awesome**

also if you put a line inside the **.gtkrc-2.0** file you can have the nice themes and fonts from gnome in awm:

include = "~/.themes/Aurora/gtk-2.0/gtkrc"

where Aurora is the name of my theme

### Post by Mateo on 2007-12-24
fbpanel seems to look almost exactly like gnome-panel, so i'm guessing it's a lot lighter on resources?

---

### Post by What is in a name? on 2007-12-24
> **Mateo said:**
> fbpanel seems to look almost exactly like gnome-panel, so i'm guessing it's a lot lighter on resources?

Basically, yes. But of course it has its own set of plugins. The GNOME panel applets, as far as I know, do not work in fbpanel, and as mentioned earlier, fbpanel does not allow much transformations in the aesthetical field beyond the GTK theme we're using. Yet it does allow alpha transparency.

### Post by Savel on 2007-12-24
> **Kingsley said:**
> That looks very nice. Can you post the conky script for me?

Here is

```

#avoid flicker

double_buffer yes



#own window to run simultanious 2 or more conkys

own_window  yes

own_window_transparent no

own_window_type normal

own_window_hints undecorate,sticky,skip_taskbar,skip_pager 



#borders

draw_borders no

border_margin 1



#shades

draw_shades no



#position

gap_x 180

gap_y 0

alignment top_left



#behaviour

update_interval 1



#colour

default_color  8f8f8f

#default_shade_color 000000

own_window_colour 262626



#font

use_xft yes

xftfont bauhaus:pixelsize=10



#to prevent window from moving

use_spacer no

minimum_size 700 0



#mpd

mpd_host localhost

mpd_port 6600



TEXT

${voffset -1} Cpu: ${color e0e0e0}${font}${cpu}% ${color} Mem: ${color e0e0e0}${font}${mem} ${color} | ${color} Up: ${color e0e0e0}${font}${uptime_short}${color}  | ${color} Net: ${color e0e0e0}${font}${downspeed eth0} Kb/s ${color} ${totaldown eth0} downloaded${color} | ${color} ${color e0e0e0}${upspeed eth0} Kb/s ${color} ${totalup eth0} uploaded${color}  |  ${color}hda1: ${color e0e0e0}${font}${fs_free /media/hda1} ${color} Savel: ${color e0e0e0}${font}${fs_free /home} ${color}

```

Enjoy..............

### Post by el mariachi on 2007-12-25
Any idea why some icons (system tray) have black backgrounds when I use white themes (all the breathe ones and other nova based themes - they use the pixmap engine)

---

### Post by urukrama on 2007-12-25
Breathe has a black panel background. Change the following line (31) in the panel.rc file:

> bg[NORMAL]        = "#040608" #Panel bg color

Change the colour to #ffffff or to anything else you'd like. Fbpanel probably uses the general gtk settings, not the panel gtk settings. Sorry for that; I rarely use a panel and spend very little time on its configuration when writing a theme.

Nice desktop btw, mariachi. I especially like the wallpaper.

---

### Post by el mariachi on 2007-12-25
Thanks urukrama!

That didn't do it. Commenting the panel bg section out did :D the theme's bg png is black it's solved thank you!

---

### Post by urukrama on 2007-12-25
> **el mariachi said:**
> That didn't do it. Commenting the panel bg section out did :D the theme's bg png is black it's solved thank you!

:) To be honest, I don't quite understand all the Gtk theme settings. I just mess around a bit and/or look at how others are doing it. If only Gtk were as easy to theme as Openbox... 

Anyway, I'm glad you got it fixed.

### Post by Salpiche on 2007-12-27
Since it is still December and I just finish another computer I thought I'll post some screen shots of my desktop.

Gnome
Emerald Theme: Tako
AWN: QV transparent, fonts Steve
Icons: Iris
I made the wallpaper a while back and never used it.
and another variation of Conky

Conky 
```
  

background yes

use_xft yes

xftfont Bitstream Vera Sans Mono:size=10

xftalpha 0.8

update_interval 1.0

total_run_times 0

own_window yes

own_window_type normal

own_window_transparent yes

own_window_hints undecorated, below, sticky, skip_taskbar, skip_pager

double_buffer yes

#minimum_size 200 5

draw_shades yes

draw_outline no

draw_borders no

draw_graph_borders yes

#stippled_borders 8

border_margin 4

border_width 1

default_color white
default_shade_color black
default_outline_color white

#alignment top_left
alignment top_right
#alignment bottom_left
#alignment bottom_right
#alignment none

gap_x 15
gap_y 35

no_buffers yes

uppercase no

cpu_avg_samples 2

net_avg_samples 2

override_utf8_locale no

use_spacer no


TEXT
${color #f1dfd6}$nodename   ${color #f1dfd6}$machine
${color #f1dfd6}$sysname $kernel 
${color #f1dfd5}$stippled_hr
${color #f1dfd6}${time %a,} ${color #f1dfd6}${time %B %e %G}
${color #f1dfd6}${time %Z,} ${color }${time %I:%M %P}
${color #f1dfd6}CPU Usage:${color #f1dfd5} $cpu% 
${color #f1dfd6}RAM Usage:$color $mem/$memmax 
${color #f1dfd6}Swap Usage:$color $swap/$swapmax 
${color #f1dfd5}$stippled_hr
${color #f1dfd6}File systems:
${color #f1dfd6}ROOT: ${color }${fs_free /}/${fs_size /}
${color #f1dfd6}HOME: ${color }${fs_free /home}/${fs_size /home}
${color #f1dfd6}STORAGE: ${color }${fs_free /media/disk-1}/${fs_size /media/disk-1}
${color #f1dfd5}$stippled_hr
${color #f1dfd6}NET: ${color}Up:${color}${upspeed ath0} k/s  ${color}Down: ${color}${downspeed ath0}k/s${color}


```

### Post by urukrama on 2007-12-27
Openbox 3.4 with the [Awakened]("http://box-look.org/content/show.php/Awakened?content=72110") Openbox theme and two versions of the Awakened Gtk theme (using the Rezlooks and Mist engines). If you have an opinion, please let me know which you think is better. I currently prefer the version in the second screenshot, but I am aware that it doesn' look very nice on some screens. The version in the third screenshot is less blue, and hopefully looks a little better on those 'other' screens.

Further details: Wallpaper is a modification of one of the wallpapers at [tenr.de]("http://tenr.de/wallpapers/wallpapers01.php?a=wallpapers") (brushed_blue). Fonts are HeldustryFTVBasic Black (window headers), Sans (Gtk and menu) and Brassfield (clock). Icons are nuoveXT-1-6. Apps shown are the Xfce theme window, Thunar, gmpc, docker (system tray) and [Lal]("http://d.minuslab.net/?p=62") (my new favourite clock).

I'm really fond of this setup. :-)

### Post by tad1073 on 2007-12-27
I reinstalled ubuntu today and had emerald themes, beryl and compiz-fusion installed. When I reinstalled compiz-fusion and emerald I lost the themes that came with emerald from the berly down load. Where can I find those themes? emerald-theme is not in synaptics. Help.

---

### Post by What is in a name? on 2007-12-27
> **Frunktz said:**
> The fonts are DejaVu?
How did you getting that settings?
In my Kubuntu I try to set that fonts, but they are same as BitStream..
I think it's a problem with AA or other some setting.

Ps:- I removed my .fonts.conf
set dpkg-reconfigure fontconfig-config
  - always
  - native
  - no

In KDE set AntiAliasing = Enabled
< RGB
FULL

But the result isn't very good as your desktop..

Just to make sure everybody gets these informations...

When I did the reconfiguration of your font settings, I chose:

Rendering: "Native"
Sub-pixel Rendering: "Always"
Bitmapped Fonts: "No"

And then, at the  GNOME Font Properties, I chose the Grayscale rendering with slight hinting. In my beloved Xfce, which I use nowadays, I have the Sub-pixel hinting disabled, and the same happens in KControl (for those KDE apps I still use; in fact, here I just chose the "System Configuration" option at the anti-aliasing section). The anti-aliasing is on, with just a slight hinting.

And why all this trouble when I could simply stick with the default settings of Gutsy? Well, this was the only way I could make my OpenOffice fonts look GOOD. Just setting the sub-pixel functions on the settings of my desktop environment will make them go back to ugliness. Oh well.

Any further doubts, just ask.

P.S.: Oh, and I forgot... I'm using Myriad for the fonts.

---

### Post by What is in a name? on 2007-12-27
> **tad1073 said:**
> I reinstalled ubuntu today and had emerald themes, beryl and compiz-fusion installed. When I reinstalled compiz-fusion and emerald I lost the themes that came with emerald from the berly down load. Where can I find those themes? emerald-theme is not in synaptics. Help.

Well, Beryl is not in the Gutsy repositories. Compiz-Fusion (with Emerald for the window decorations, of course) is the default now. The "good" old Compiz with plugins from Beryl. To mix both is not advised. So, assuming you are not using third-party repos, do you have all dependencies satisfied? Is libemeraldengine0 installed as well, for example?

---

### Post by Gigamo on 2007-12-27
> **What is in a name? said:**
> Just to make sure everybody gets these informations...

When I did the reconfiguration of your font settings, I chose:

Rendering: "Native"
Sub-pixel Rendering: "Always"
Bitmapped Fonts: "No"

And then, at the  GNOME Font Properties, I chose the Grayscale rendering with slight hinting. In my beloved Xfce, which I use nowadays, I have the Sub-pixel hinting disabled, and the same happens in KControl (for those KDE apps I still use; in fact, here I just chose the "System Configuration" option at the anti-aliasing section). The anti-aliasing is on, with just a slight hinting.

And why all this trouble when I could simply stick with the default settings of Gutsy? Well, this was the only way I could make my OpenOffice fonts look GOOD. Just setting the sub-pixel functions on the settings of my desktop environment will make them go back to ugliness. Oh well.

Any further doubts, just ask.

P.S.: Oh, and I forgot... I'm using Myriad for the fonts.

Hmmm, I love the way your fonts are setup but I've run into a little problem. I have all the Myriad Pro fonts on my windows/fonts directory, and I changed them into .ttf's so I could install them and update my fonts cache. But when I select the font in gnome's appearance manager, I just get rectangles for every case (the font doesn't work). How did you do it? Should also mention that when i go to the fonts:/// folder, the myriad fonts have some additional 'icons' on them; some have a cross and others have a lock. 

Thanks!

### Post by Gigamo on 2007-12-27
> **What is in a name? said:**
> Good, that would be my next suggestion. Did you choose any specific option in FontForge beyond the basic change from OpenType to TrueType?

And furthermore, have you rebooted since you installed the fonts? Sometimes, for some reason, I encountered some problems because the whole system (or at least the desktop environment...) needed to reload in order to properly use the fonts.

I have not rebooted yet. I did reload the DE already though.

I used fontforge using a script: 

```
#!/usr/local/bin/fontforge
# Quick and dirty hack: converts a font to truetype (.ttf)
Print("Opening "+$1);
Open($1);
Print("Saving "+$1:r+".ttf");
Generate($1:r+".ttf");
Quit(0);
```

And then ran 
```
fontforge -script otf2ttf.sh FONTNAME.otf
```

Edit: I now also rebooted with no luck.

### Post by What is in a name? on 2007-12-27
> **Gigamo said:**
> Meh, that's gonna be alot of work seeing how many variations Myriad Pro has :D

Do you think singly converting Myriad Pro (the regular one) will do the trick? or do they all depend on eachother?

It will not be that hard... Once you put your conscious mind asleep and automatize your gestures, you can do it all in 7-8 minutes. The thing is that changing one weight of a font alone will not affect the others. You will have Myriad Regular available and then as soon as you need its Bold variation all you get is Bitstream again in the screen or whatever.

### Post by BattlePanic on 2007-12-28
> **urukrama said:**
> Same as before, but now, thanks to [K.Mandla]("http://kmandla.wordpress.com/2007/12/27/still-better-font-smoothing/") with much better looking fonts.

urukrama,

How did you get the Openbox menu to display it's submenus so that they are horizontally aligned with their parent menu item?  By default Openbox seems to cascade submenus downward by a pixel or two.

---

### Post by urukrama on 2007-12-28
> **BattlePanic said:**
> urukrama,

How did you get the Openbox menu to display it's submenus so that they are horizontally aligned with their parent menu item?  By default Openbox seems to cascade submenus downward by a pixel or two.

That is set in the themerc file of the theme you are using (either in */usr/share/themes/THEMENAME/opebox-3/themerc* or */home/USERNAME/.themes/THEMENAME/opebox-3/themerc*)

Look for the following line: > menu.overlap: *NUMBER*

The number following it is the amount in which the submenu overlaps its parent menu. If you set 1 it will overlap 1 pixel, but also be offset by 1 pixel. If you set -1 it will be one pixel removed from the parent menu but also one pixel offset upwards. If you set it to 0 there is no offset and overlap, as in my screenshot.

Change the setting of the theme you are using to what you want and reconfigure openbox (in the right click desktop menu). The changes should be visible.

Some themes come with a menu overlap and others don't. In any case it is easy to change. I hope this helps.

---

### Post by PurposeOfReason on 2007-12-28
> **Gigamo said:**
> Could you post your .conkyrc file / compiz theme? :p
**Conky**
```
background yes
cpu_avg_samples 2
net_avg_samples 2
out_to_console no
use_xft yes
xftfont Unbatang:size=7
xftalpha 0.8
mail_spool $MAIL
update_interval 1
own_window yes
own_window_type override
own_window_transparent yes
own_window_hints undecorated,below,sticky,skip_taskbar,skip_pager
double_buffer yes
minimum_size 145 2
maximum_width 145 2
draw_shades no
draw_outline no
draw_borders no
stippled_borders no
border_margin 1
border_width 1
gap_x 5
gap_y 5
alignment bottom_right
use_spacer no
no_buffers yes
uppercase no
mpd_host localhost
mpd_port 6600

TEXT
${color #98c2c7}${time %l:%M}$color${alignr}${time %a,} ${time %B %e}
${color #b1b1b1}POWER ${hr 2}$color
${color #98c2c7}Core One:$color     ${alignr}${cpu cpu1}%
${color #98c2c7}Core Two:$color     ${alignr}${cpu cpu2}%
${color #98c2c7}Memory:$color       ${alignr}$memperc%
${color #98c2c7}Power:$color     ${alignr}${battery_percent}%
${color #98c2c7}AC:$color     ${alignr}${acpiacadapter}
${color #98c2c7}${cpugraph 20,145 98c2c7}
${color #b1b1b1}FILESYSTEM ${hr 2}$color
${color #98c2c7}Archlinux:$color ${alignr}${fs_used_perc /}%
${color #98c2c7}Vista:$color       ${alignr}${fs_used_perc /vista}%
${color #b1b1b1}NETWORK ${hr 2}$color
${color #98c2c7}Upload:$color     ${alignr}${upspeed wlan0}kb/s${color #98c2c7}
${color #98c2c7}Download:$color ${alignr}${downspeed wlan0}kb/s${color #98c2c7}
${color #98c2c7}Gmail:$color ${alignr}${texeci 90 python /home/shawn/.scripts/gmail.py}
${color #98c2c7}Wireless:$color ${alignr}${wireless_link_qual_perc wlan0}
${color #b1b1b1}MUSIC ${hr 2}$color
${color #98c2c7}Status:$color     ${alignr}${mpd_status}
${color #98c2c7}Time:$color     ${alignr}${mpd_elapsed}/${mpd_length}${color #98c2c7}
${color #98c2c7}Song:$color     ${alignr}${mpd_title}${color #98c2c7}
```
**Emerald**
[Link](http://www.fileshost.com/en/file/24025/Minimal-emerald.html)
Be warned, there are no buttons. :)

### Post by Gigamo on 2007-12-28
> **PurposeOfReason said:**
> What script are you using?

I'm using this one:

```
import os

import string



#Enter your username and password below within double quotes

# eg. username="username" and password="password"

username="my username"

password="my password"



com="wget -O - https://"+username+":"+password+"@mail.google.com/mail/feed/atom --no-check-certificate"



temp=os.popen(com)

msg=temp.read()

index=string.find(msg,"<fullcount>")

index2=string.find(msg,"</fullcount>")

fc=int(msg[index+11:index2])



if fc==0:

   print "0 new"

else:

   print str(fc)+" new"
```

### Post by PurposeOfReason on 2007-12-28
Try this one. Don't forget to make it executable.
```
import os
import string
#Enter your username and password below within double quotes
# eg. username="username" and password="password"
username="PUTUSERNAMEHERE"
password="PUTPASSWORDHERE"
ttext=""
title=""
ntext=[]
nam=[]
mtext=[]
mes=[]
sum=[]
ema=[]
nom=""
tot=0
rtot=0
com="wget -O - https://"+username+":"+password+"@mail.google.com/mail/feed/atom --no-check-certificate"
temp=os.popen(com)
msg=temp.read()
index = string.find(msg,"<title>")
index2=string.find(msg,"</title>")  
title=msg[index+25:index2]
index=index2
index=string.find(msg,"<fullcount>")
index2=string.find(msg,"</fullcount>")
fc=msg[index+11:index2]
if(int(fc)>20):tot=20
else: tot=(int(fc))
rtot=tot
if (int(fc)==1):
   print ""+fc+" new"
elif rtot==0:
   print "0 new"
elif rtot>1:
   print ""+fc+" new"
else:
   print "Woops!!!"
```

---

### Post by urukrama on 2007-12-29
Nice one, mariachi.

I've been using Pekwm again, and made it my default window manger for now. It is really great. Very light and fast, very configurable (how many window managers allow you to edit the window menu (close, maximize, etc) to your liking?). 

Here are the details: Pekwm 0.1.5 with my own yet unnamed theme. Gtk theme is my own Awakened (yet unreleased), icons are nuoveXT-1.6, fonts are Sans. The wallpaper uses a modified tile that was posted in this thread (if my memory serves me well). Applications running are Terminal (Xfce), pypanel, Thunar, Gmpc, and xpad.

### Post by sjnims on 2007-12-29
WHAT YOU SEE:
-Default theme with ATI driver enabled and compiz-fusion running
-conky formatted just the way I like it

FOR ME TO DO:
-Add a theme
-Play around with the colors for conky

Any suggestions?

Attached is the weather.sh script file and the weather.xslt file saved as a text document (couldn't upload the *.xslt file) originally from [http://pondol.com/weather.tar.gz](http://pondol.com/weather.tar.gz).

My conkyrc file:
```
# Conky configuration
#
# the list of variables has been removed from this file in favour
# of keeping the documentation more maintainable.
# Check http://conky.sf.net for an up-to-date-list.

# set to yes if you want Conky to be forked in the background
background no

# X font when Xft is disabled, you can pick one with program xfontsel
#font 5x7
#font 6x10
#font 7x13
#font 8x13
#font 9x15
#font *mintsmild.se*
#font -*-*-*-*-*-*-34-*-*-*-*-*-*-*

# Use Xft?
use_xft yes

# Xft font when Xft is enabled
xftfont Bitstream Vera Sans Mono:size=10

# Text alpha when using Xft
xftalpha 0.8

# Print everything to stdout?
# out_to_console no

# MPD host/port
# mpd_host localhost
# mpd_port 6600
# mpd_password tinker_bell

# Print everything to console?
# out_to_console no

# mail spool
mail_spool $MAIL

# Update interval in seconds
update_interval 1.0

# This is the number of times Conky will update before quitting.
# Set to zero to run forever.
total_run_times 0

# Create own window instead of using desktop (required in nautilus)
own_window no

# If own_window is yes, you may use type normal, desktop or override
#own_window_type desktop

# Use pseudo transparency with own_window?
own_window_transparent yes

# If own_window_transparent is set to no, you can set the background colour here
own_window_colour hotpink

# If own_window is yes, these window manager hints may be used
#own_window_hints undecorated,below,sticky,skip_taskbar,skip_pager

# Use double buffering (reduces flicker, may not work for everyone)
double_buffer yes

# Minimum size of text area
minimum_size 280 5

# Draw shades?
draw_shades yes

# Draw outlines?
draw_outline no

# Draw borders around text
draw_borders no

# Draw borders around graphs
draw_graph_borders yes

# Stippled borders?
stippled_borders 8

# border margins
border_margin 4

# border width
border_width 1

# Default colors and also border colors
default_color white
default_shade_color black
default_outline_color black

#dexter_client no
#dexter_server no
# config file for libdexter (default search path: $HOME/.dexterrc; /etc/libdexter/dexter.conf)
#dexter_config

# Text alignment, other possible values are commented
#alignment top_left
alignment top_right
#alignment bottom_left
#alignment bottom_right
#alignment none

# Gap between borders of screen and text
# same thing as passing -x at command line
#gap_x 24
gap_y 24

# Subtract file system buffers from used memory?
no_buffers yes

# set to yes if you want all text to be in uppercase
uppercase no

# number of cpu samples to average
# set to 1 to disable averaging
cpu_avg_samples 2

# number of net samples to average
# set to 1 to disable averaging
net_avg_samples 2

# Force UTF8? note that UTF8 support required XFT
override_utf8_locale no

# Add spaces to keep things from moving about?  This only affects certain objects.
use_spacer no

# Allow each port monitor to track at most this many connections (if 0 or not set, default is 256)
#max_port_monitor_connections 256

# Maximum number of special things, e.g. fonts, offsets, aligns, etc.
#max_specials 512

# Maximum size of buffer for user text, i.e. below TEXT line.
#max_user_text 16384

# variable is given either in format $variable or in ${variable}. Latter
# allows characters right after the variable and must be used in network
# stuff because of an argument

# stuff after 'TEXT' will be formatted on screen

TEXT
System ${hr 2}  
  Ubuntu $sysname $kernel on $nodename
  Uptime$alignr$uptime
CPU ${hr 2}
  Usage $alignr $cpu%
  Frequency$alignr${freq_dyn_g 0}GHz
  ${cpugraph 32}
Memory ${hr 2}
  $mem/$memmax$alignr$memperc%
  ${membar 8}
Temperatures ${hr 2}
  CPU $alignr ${i2c temp 2}C (${i2c tempf 2}F)
  MB $alignr ${i2c temp 1}C (${i2c tempf 1}F)
Fans ${hr 2}
  CPU Fan$alignr${i2c fan 1} RPM
  Case Fan 1$alignr${i2c fan 2} RPM
  Case Fan 2$alignr${i2c fan 5} RPM
  PSU Fan$alignr${i2c fan 3} RPM
File Systems ${hr 2}
  /$alignc${fs_used /}/${fs_size /}${alignr}${fs_used_perc /}%
  ${fs_bar 8 /}
  /home$alignc${fs_used /home}/${fs_size /home}${alignr}${fs_used_perc /home}%
  ${fs_bar 8 /home}
  /swap$alignc$swap/$swapmax$alignr$swapperc%
  ${swapbar 8}
Network ${hr 2}
  IP$alignr${addr wlan0}
  Upload ${upspeed wlan0}kb/s ${alignr}Download ${downspeed wlan0}kb/s
  ${upspeedgraph wlan0 32,150}${alignr}${downspeedgraph wlan0 32,150}
Weather ${hr 2}
  ${execi 120 /home/steve/scripts/weather/weather.sh XXXXX}
```

[[IMG]http://img247.imageshack.us/img247/8561/conkyjk6.th.png[/IMG]](http://img247.imageshack.us/my.php?image=conkyjk6.png)

[[IMG]http://img80.imageshack.us/img80/711/screenwl3.th.png[/IMG]](http://img80.imageshack.us/my.php?image=screenwl3.png)
